The tortillas were like store bought. Not fresh, or made there. At least, they didn't taste like it. They had cilantro and onion on them. They were good. Basic tacos.

<Rate>5</Rate>< text>
I ordered three tacos; chicken, carnitas and al pastor. The seasoning was perfect for me (spice wuss); mildly spicy with a ton of flavor. Yum! We also ordered chips, salsa and guacamole. The guac came with slices of radishes (as did the tacos and burrito) and it was a minor revelation for me. I never realized how well radishes paired with Mexican food before! Amazing! The restaurant interior is narrow with about 5 (?) small tables, clean and neat. The woman who took our order was warm and welcoming. The food was delicious and reasonably priced and there is lots of available parking. We'll definitely be back!<//text>

Wow. I must say this is one of the best Mexican spots I've ever had. <Review>We are still in mourning over the closure of our beloved Hacienda Grill in Richmond.  We ate there for all 16 years of its existence, Their food was delicious.

We are searching for a New Mexican place that offers delicious food at reasonable prices.

So last week we decided to try La Gran Chiquita for lunch.

I got a chicken torta ($9.95) and Mr Rinky got a veggie burrito.
The torta was tasty with tender chicken, lettuce, onion, tomatoes and mayo. I liked it but not the best I've had.

Mr Rinky liked his veggie burrito--beans, rice, lettuce, tomato and guacamole.  No roasted vegetables.

You order at the counter and are served at your table.  The counter person was very warm and friendly.  The salsa bar was EXCELLENT--
four kinds of salsa, radishes and a few other toppings I forgot   about.
Serve yourself chips.  I love being able to help myself to salsa and chips.

There were a few other customers--two families with young children,
some solo diners and some take out folks.

The restaurant is large.  The bathrooms are clean and large also.

I think we may return but in the meantime we'll be checking out some more places.</Review><username>Dave Evans</username>< Pics>

<Text>The rice is amazing at this place, simply delicious. But the decor is a bit tacky and the one man band is way too loud. Sure, that's what's normal for a Mexican Restaurant but you can barely hear yourself as the music echoes in the 97 percent empty room. I'm not sure why the musician would ask the people who are the least likely to know any spanish music, what song he should play next. We shake our head and explain we dont know any and he just keeps asking. Anyways, the service here is good. They get to your table quick, and return often which is nice. The only thing that I would add that disappoints me is the way they serve the carnitas. They cube it rather than have it shredded. I'm not sure if that's an idea they have to stand out as a restaurant but it makes it taste weird and bland. 1600377179447<//Date>
< Review>
Dona Bibi's was my first time having Honduran food. It's out in LA next to MacArthur Park in Westlake. This places is run by an amazing family. They are Honduran and bring that authentic, traditional recipe to the foods. I had the baleadas (which are their Honduran style tortillas), which was pretty good. I also ate their sopa mixta, the conch meat soup with coconut milk, which was also very tasty, especially if you love seafood. The Honduran style fried chicken was also great here, loved the sauce that was over it. And I got to try many of their appetizers on their sampler plate which had everything from the pastelitos (fried empanadas) to tacos dorados (kind of like a taquito).

Overall, I would recommend this restaurant. The food was fresh, it had great taste, and the service was wonderful. This restaurant will give you a great first impression of Honduran food if you've never had it before. I shot a YouTube video of Dona Bibi's which you can find on my channel, Rockstar Eater< /Review>
